  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/19836795?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K" href="/user/show/373260-k">K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781427201003" href="/book/show/1470107.The_Religion">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">mel gibson fans, davinci code people?</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/373260-k?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/373260-k?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19836795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12489232058048679091">Have just started disc 1 of this 21 disc audiobook. I could see this not working out. The longest audiobook I've previously listened to was 10 discs, and that took forever! This one's started out promisingly enough, though, with the most violent opening scenes I have ever read/heard. It's like the climaxes of five Gibson movies compressed into five minutes. <br/><br/>Okay, done: <br/>The parallels to Mel Gibson movies carry out the whole way through. Ridiculous amounts of violence, lusty swiving, stupid stereo</span>
  <span id="freeText12489232058048679091" style="display:none">Have just started disc 1 of this 21 disc audiobook. I could see this not working out. The longest audiobook I've previously listened to was 10 discs, and that took forever! This one's started out promisingly enough, though, with the most violent opening scenes I have ever read/heard. It's like the climaxes of five Gibson movies compressed into five minutes. <br /><br />Okay, done: <br />The parallels to Mel Gibson movies carry out the whole way through. Ridiculous amounts of violence, lusty swiving, stupid stereotypes wrapped in sanctimonious language, and characters introduced only for the purpose of killing them later. Still, Mel Gibson movies can be plenty entertaining, and I have paid to watch more than a couple in the theater. Would definitely recommend NOT listening to this on audiotape, though. Listened to 13 discs and then read the rest, and the audiotape made the book seem five times more obnoxious.<br /><br />Anyhoo, The Religion's about Mattias Tannauser, an East Hungarian blacksmith's son turned Turkish Janissary turned soldier-of-Fortune, whose every appearance into any given setting stirs admiration in the hearts of men and lust in the bellies of women. This supposed baddest badass of all time becomes involved with a noblewoman named Carla who's looking for her long-lost son, the fruit of her teenage affair with a priest turned High Catholic Inquisitor, Ludovico. So Mattias agrees to take her to Malta, where she thinks her son is located, even though it's about to be attacked by the Turks, and they all end up trapped there during the Great 1565 Siege of Malta. This was apparently one of the bloodiest sieges in history, and the Religion is all about the grossest realities of the event: sword wounds, intestines falling out, brains bashed in, eyeballs gouged, faces sliced off, everybody pooping everywhere (seriously, it seems like Willocks was trying to describe every pooping incident that occurred during the siege), animals suffering, sepsis, beheadings, etc. etc. etc. <br /><br />The writing is serviceable. There are some shallow attempts at lyricism and profundity. Again, I probably would have enjoyed it better had I just read it in a gulp rather than listened to it over a period of weeks. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12489232058048679091" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1121692664" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1121692664" />
    <a title="Michael Flanagan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3789573-michael-flanagan"><img alt="Michael Flanagan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469675533p2/3789573.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1121692664?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Flanagan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Flanagan" href="/user/show/3789573-michael-flanagan">Michael Flanagan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1121692664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4277894152378015799">Never has a book given me such joy & pain as The Religion. Tim Willocks delivers a real mixed bag that sits on the precipice of an epic with the wasteland of mediocrity spreading out below.<br/><br/>So let’s have a look at what I liked about this book. I loved the characters as they were well fleshed out, each with their own back story that could easily become a book in their own right. The historical context was spot on with enough information given to let you get a good sense of the times. The action wa</span>
  <span id="freeText4277894152378015799" style="display:none">Never has a book given me such joy &amp; pain as The Religion. Tim Willocks delivers a real mixed bag that sits on the precipice of an epic with the wasteland of mediocrity spreading out below.<br /><br />So let’s have a look at what I liked about this book. I loved the characters as they were well fleshed out, each with their own back story that could easily become a book in their own right. The historical context was spot on with enough information given to let you get a good sense of the times. The action was fast and brutal without getting bogged down with a blow by blow report. At times the story flew right off the page and had me reading in a state of great excitement.<br /><br />Now it is time for what I did not like about The Religion. This book is so, so, so long. Which is not by itself a bad thing, but boy can this author prattle on. I found myself at times during this book not caring about what was going on. Several times I nearly chucked up my hands in surrender to walk away never to return. This book in my humble opinion could have shed 200 odd pages without detracting from the story.<br /><br />The Religion for me was far from an enlightening read. A real life Jekyll and Hide, combining what I love and detest about reading all in one book. Make sure you prepare before committing to this read. Because once you set off there is no turning back you are in for the long haul. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4277894152378015799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_55040766" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/55040766" />
    <a title="Janet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1162386-janet"><img alt="Janet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1226430162p2/1162386.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/55040766?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janet" href="/user/show/1162386-janet">Janet</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55040766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer587645338001047551">It's been a long time since I read an historical novel that was truly a "page turner" -- but once I got into this story I hated to put it down. <br/><br/>As is always the case for me, the heart of the appeal of the story lies with the characters, and I enjoyed spending time with all the protagonists. Equally importantly, the primary villain was compelling: both frightening and just a bit tragic. The conflicting cultures of Christian Knights of St. John ("the Hospitallers") and the armies of Islam were bot</span>
  <span id="freeText587645338001047551" style="display:none">It's been a long time since I read an historical novel that was truly a "page turner" -- but once I got into this story I hated to put it down. <br /><br />As is always the case for me, the heart of the appeal of the story lies with the characters, and I enjoyed spending time with all the protagonists. Equally importantly, the primary villain was compelling: both frightening and just a bit tragic. The conflicting cultures of Christian Knights of St. John ("the Hospitallers") and the armies of Islam were both portrayed with due regard for their mutual virtues and weaknesses, and the varying degrees to which they were present in individuals. <br /><br />Author Willocks is both a doctor and a martial artists, and his experiences in those fields lend vivid detail to his descriptions of the unholy thrill of war and the specifics of the carnage it leaves behind. In fact, the one fault of the book is that he spends far too much time dwelling on the bloody details, and I skimmed over paragraph after paragraph of such details when I was about halfway through the book.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="587645338001047551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_908811825" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/908811825" />
    <a title="Louise Roberts" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30299315-louise-roberts"><img alt="Louise Roberts" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506448148p2/30299315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/908811825?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Louise Roberts" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Louise Roberts" href="/user/show/30299315-louise-roberts">Louise Roberts</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer908811825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9629819365438258595">This is one of the best books I have ever read. I enjoyed it so much I have re-read it four times.<br/><br/>Tim Willocks has thoroughly researched his material thus drawing the reader into his story to the extent that one feels as though actually present within the pages. I found myself visualising the hero - Mattias Tannhauser - and was with him during the epic siege of Malta. And when he was with his lover I felt an intruder during their intimate moments. But I found I was too drawn to the delicateness </span>
  <span id="freeText9629819365438258595" style="display:none">This is one of the best books I have ever read. I enjoyed it so much I have re-read it four times.<br /><br />Tim Willocks has thoroughly researched his material thus drawing the reader into his story to the extent that one feels as though actually present within the pages. I found myself visualising the hero - Mattias Tannhauser - and was with him during the epic siege of Malta. And when he was with his lover I felt an intruder during their intimate moments. But I found I was too drawn to the delicateness of their moments together to close my eyes and allow them the privacy they deserved, and I shared their togetherness with respectful tenderness.<br /><br />The story drew you into their lives; it made you feel strong, yet compassionate. Determined, even understanding at the conflict within the hero's soul as he tried to do the right thing by others even at his own expense.<br /><br />The Religion is a book you can never put down, and when you finally read "The End" you take in a deep breath and start reading it all over again.<br /><br />Louise Roberts</span>
  <a data-text-id="9629819365438258595" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mMzHPSCRcXQx3RxpWfH2wel1u4V0ekunVXF4WCnkBlCZ/+BD6bavf4vJFv/dYRzFTG+VJl3RjpeY5zY1DIjE8g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

Pressfield has created a cast of extraordinarily vivid characters, from the unforgettable Selene, whose surrender to the Greeks does nothing to tame her; to her lover, Damon, an Athenian warrior who grows to cherish the wild Amazon ways; to the narrator, Bones, a young girl from a noble family who was nursed by Selene from birth and secretly taught the Amazon way; to the great Theseus, the tragic king; and to Antiope, the noble queen who betrayed tal Kyrte for the love of Theseus.\n\nWith astounding immediacy and extraordinary attention to military detail, Pressfield transports readers into the heat and terror of war. Equally impressive is his creation of the Amazon nation, its people, its rituals and myths, its greatness and savagery. Last of the Amazons is thrilling on every page, an epic tale of the clash between wildness and civilization, patriotism and love, man and woman.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"2147548260734153145\"       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/903169-the-religion">Quotes from The Religion</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Her eyes were of different colors, the left as brown as autumn, the right as gray as Atlantic wind. Both seemed alive with questions that would never be voiced, as if no words yet existed with which to frame them. She was nineteen years old, or thereabouts; her exact age was unknown. Her face was as fresh as an apple and as delicate as blossom, but a marked depression in the bones beneath her left eye gave her features a disturbing asymmetry. Her mouth never curved into a smile. God, it seemed, had withheld that possibility, as surely as from a blind man the power of sight. He had withheld much else. Amparo was touched—by genius, by madness, by the Devil, or by a conspiracy of all these and more. She took no sacraments and appeared incapable of prayer. She had a horror of clocks and mirrors. By her own account she spoke with Angels and could hear the thoughts of animals and trees. She was passionately kind to all living things. She was a beam of starlight trapped in flesh and awaiting only the moment when it would continue on its journey into forever.” (p.33)&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/446589-her-eyes-were-of-different-colors-the-left-as-brown">53 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Sadness is never bad," said Amparo. "Sadness is the mirror of being happy&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;

        script.async = true;
        script.src = load[i];
        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>
